B003VANOFY|3.0|I've been using this headset for a few weeks now, and my experiences are a bit of a mixed bag. I'm not a big fan of Logitech's products, and was weary about all the negative feedback I saw on this product in particular, but it seemed like a good value for a wireless headset.    The good:  -Surround sound and overall sound quality are pretty good  -The around-ear headphones dampen most outside sounds, while not completely deafening you to your surroundings  -Battery life averages 6-8 hours  -Wireless connection is excellent    The bad:  All of these issues emerged after 2-3 weeks of use.  -significant response lag when using the side volume wheel (I adjust the volume, but it can take 5-10 seconds to actually change volume)  -Slight buzzing noise (as reported by many others) when near max volume. For me, this isn't much of an issue, as I see little reason to have the volume this high in the first place, but it's worth mentioning.  -Odd behavior with low battery life when on the charger: Basically after being on the charger all day, it sometimes (inconsistently) begins a loud buzzing/siren sound, and then shuts off after 20-30 seconds, as if it died. It must be left off for several minutes before it will turn on normally again, at which point it shows a full charge. Additionally, the sound volume can randomly cut out, to the point where you have to be at max volume to hear at the same level as say, 25% volume.  -Surround sound no longer seems to function at all (I have not yet attempted to fix this, it's probably just driver issues)    All in all, it's not that bad of a headset, though it's worth noting that it is my first wireless one. The technical issues seem fairly severe, and make the set seem a little shoddy. If you've had good experiences with logitech, this might be a reasonable purchase, but otherwise I'd recommend researching some other options.    EDIT:  I wrote this review about two years ago. I'd like to add some information about my experiences.  First, Ihave used 3 of these so far. The charging port is VERY fragile and poorly connected. If you begin losing sound in the right side, it is a loose mini-usb port. If you have the tools and the steady hand, you can repair it yourself. I bought a second headset which also broke (both after 1 year of use) and the third was a warranty return.   Second, if you have a spare wall outlet, prefer to charge from there. The PC charging tends to only prolong the inevitable battery drainage.   Third, don't wear it while plugged in unless you must. The charge port will last much longer this way.    I still love this headset, but it's important to be aware of the potential faults, otherwise you may find yourself ordering one of these yearly.

In fact, it changed my life so dramatically that I am now dedicating my professional life to evangelizing this nutrient-dense way of eating and helping other people recover from a life on the Standard American Diet (SAD).<br /><br />It Starts with Food is written in a friendly, non judgmental yet firm tone. They're not saying a food is \\"off limits\\" but teaching you how to make better choices. \\"There is not guilt with food, just consequences\\" according to Melissa and Dallas. They're not saying you \\"can't\\" eat certain foods on special occasions, like drinking some wine at a friend's wedding. What they're saying is that food will either make you \\"more healthy or less healthy\\". They very clearly explain how your body's hormones work in response to food in a healthy and unhealthy situation. Their science is solid. You can dive into it and understand more than most doctors about human nutrient metabolism, or you can skip to chapter 8 where they dive into which foods are optimal for our bodies.<br /><br />In the \\"Meal Map\\" section at the end of the book, I really enjoyed how they chart out master recipes to \\"teach\\" you HOW to cook instead of lengthy complicated recipes. Basically, you take some animal protein, add vegetables, good fats and some seasonings and there you have it. I also like how they break down breakfast lunch and dinner into \\"Meals 1, 2 & 3\\". B007L96VCY|5.0|In May 1971, in the wake of an ongoing string of Beatles post-breakup solo albums (Paul's April 1970 [[ASIN:B004WJRF6C McCartney (Archive Collection)]], John's December 1970 [[ASIN:B003Y8YXFI Plastic Ono Band]], George's November 1970 [[ASIN:B00005214X All Things Must Pass [BOXED EDITION]]], Ringo's September 1970 [[ASIN:B000006N4I Beaucoups of Blues]]), most critics converged on one simple point of discussion...\\"When are The Beatles going to get back together?\\"<br /><br />Unless you count the George, Paul & Ringo participation in the \\"Anthology\\" documentary, we all know the answer to that question...\\"never.\\"<br /><br />So in 2012, I reject the idea that \\"Ram\\" (or any other Beatles solo album) is a \\"lost\\" classic. A more accurate assessment is that in 1970 & 1971...when the breakup was still a \\"fresh wound\\"...audiences and critics were listening with one ear. These were \\"yeah, but...\\" albums, as in \\"Yeah, I like some of the songs on \\"Ram,\\" but I wish The Beatles would get back together.\\"<br /><br />With the benefit of hindsight (and fresh remastering) we can now see that this solo album, actually billed as \\"Paul and Linda McCartney,\\" was in fact a very strong follow-up to the \\"McCartney\\" album, and a work rich in Paul's best Beatle-isms. It really is a monor hop, skip & jump from the [[ASIN:B0025KVLTM Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band]] track \\"She's Leaving Home\\" to \\"Back Seat of My Car.\\" \\"Uncle Albert / Admiral Halsey\\" is another Sir Paul suite / mini-epic, along the lines of the [[ASIN:B0025KVLUQ Abbey Road (Remastered)]] \\"You Never Give Me Your Money\\" song arc. \\"Smile Away\\" is a goof, cut from the same cloth as \\"Why Don't We Do It In The Road\\" with faux-Doo Wop background vocals, crunchy guitars, and off-the wall lyrics. You get a few more acoustic / rustic numbers in the \\"McCartney\\" vein like \\"Dear Boy\\" (supposedly a \\"message\\" to John that contributed to his \\"response\\" of \\"How Do You Sleep At Night\\" four months later on [[ASIN:B003Y8YXFS Imagine]]) and \\"Heart of the Country.\\"<br /><br />As rich and textured as it is, more than a few 1971 critics dismissed \\"Ram\\" as being \\"lightweight,\\" but that's probably because they didn't know Paul as going to unleash the first Wings album, [[ASIN:B00000DQYR Wings Wild Life]], in December of that year...probably his single most \\"lightweight\\" album to date with throw-away confections like \\"Mumbo\\" and \\"Bip Bop.\\"<br /><br />The reason \\"Ram\\" sounds so good in 2012...remastering aside...is that we didn't give it an objective listen in 1971. It was very, very good...perhaps even great...but we wanted The Beatles, even if Paul, John, George and Ringo did not.<br /><br />It's sweet, heartfelt, and in some places it rocks. It was good then, it's good now...an essential addition to your music library.t of the Country.\\"<br /><br />As rich and textured as it is, more than a few 1971 critics dismissed \\"Ram\\" as being \\"lightweight,\\" but that's probably because they didn't know Paul as going to unleash the first Wings album, [[ASIN:B00000DQYR Wings Wild Life]], in December of that year...probably his single most \\"lightweight\\" album to date with throw-away confections like \\"Mumbo\\" and \\"Bip Bop.\\"<br /><br />The reason \\"Ram\\" sounds so good in 2012...remastering aside...is that we didn't give it an objective listen in 1971. B000FC130E|4.0|\\"Neverwhere\\" is an urban fantasy novel by Neil Gaiman.  It tells the story of Richard, an average man in a dysfunctional relationship with his overbearing girlfriend.  One day, Richard stumbles upon a bleeding girl lying upon a sidewalk.  His decision to help her is life changing, as he finds himself sucked into the nightmarish wonderland of London Below.  London Below is inhabited by those individuals who fell through the cracks of society (and reality itself), and once Richard begins to see its denizens, he becomes invisible to people in the world above.  He follows the girl whom he rescued, whose name is Door, in the hopes of finding his way home, only to discover that Door's life is threatened by the same people who murdered her family.<br /><br />...and the villains!  Croup and Vandemar are a pair of bumbling but humorous mercenary bad guys who enjoy their job far too much.  You can't hate them, because it's very hard to take one's villains seriously when they're trying to talk with a mouth full of toads.<br /><br />The atmosphere of London Below is one of the biggest strengths of this book.  Gaiman is able to draw on both the mundane and the absurd to create a world that is simultaneously beautiful and menacing.<br /><br />One of the weaknesses of \\"Neverwhere\\" is the general lack of character development throughout the novel.  Most of the characters don't change, but Richard's perspective on them does, so I'll forgive it.  Most of the characters in London Below are unabashedly themselves.  Characters represent different archetypes and seem to have come out of a fairy tale, but one of the overreaching themes of the novel is that life isn't always what it seems and that there is more to people than meets the eye.  The minor characters are extremely memorable, such as the Amazonian woman named Hunter who is searching for a fabled Beast or the Old Bailey who talks to birds and trades in favors.<br /><br />Overall, I'd highly recommend this book.  It reminds me of a darker version of Alice in Wonderland, but in a more modern setting complete with subway rats, floating markets, and plenty of hidden dangers.  Even though the book has some flaws, the story is enjoyable and imaginative.a darker version of Alice in Wonderland, but in a more modern setting complete with subway rats, floating markets, and plenty of hidden dangers.  Even though the book has some flaws, the story is enjoyable and imaginative.

I did notice, and you should as well, that when choosing the audio setup in the menu, on the upper left of the screen there is a round target that you also need to arrow up to to engage the discreet channeling to its maximum.  This is the second time I have seen something like this on a disc and I think it is simple a stupid function.  You should be able to simply chose the audio mix you want and play the movie but in this case, setting the proper audio is a two step process.  Without doing the second step you will not get the full surround you were hoping for.<br /><br />I have seen this film many times.  I find it fun and not to be taken seriously.<br />All my movie reviews are of this nature and focus only on the quality of the transfer to BluRay so check them and see if they are of help as well.<br />Hopefully, this review has been of some help to you in determining your purchase, hope I am on the correct path with a review of the transfer quality as opposed to providing plot summaries.<br />Thanksa review of the transfer quality as opposed to providing plot summaries.<br />Thanks

It has been in the family for generations (hence the title) and most of Matt's relatives want to sell the land and make millions. Matt is going along with it but part of him wonders if they're doing a disservice to later generations in the family.<br /><br />But the real catalyst is when Matt's wife has a major boating accident and is in the hospital with a coma and Matt believes she is going to come out of it and then the doctor tells him it isn't going to happen and he needs to tell the whole family that she will be dead soon. That's when the poignant moments come into this movie which are most likely the major reason it was so well received by the critics. Add to that a dysfunctional family with secrets and you start to see everything unravel but you also get these strange moments where you can't help laughing or maybe laughing but still feeling their pain. At one point Matt tells his eldest daughter that their mother isn't going to make it (he does it clumsily at best) and the daughter submerges into the pool holding her breathe and the camera spends an inordinate amount of time focused on her facial grief. What follows is a journey with his two daughters and a guy friend of the eldest named Sid to confront the real estate man but to also come to terms with their grief, unsaid words to the mother/wife in a coma and their overall place in the universe. This is a definite soul searching movie on several levels. There are a few moments of clarity in which they have these revealing conversations. The eldest daughter lashes out in her rage at times, especially towards what her mother has done to the family, and the youngest daughter knows something is wrong so she goes off into dramatic situations to get attention.<br /><br />Themes about forgiveness versus vengeance when your spouse cheats on you are obvious. What type of person would you be and the film suggests you really do not know until it happens. Additionally, there's a definite thematic focus on how weird family can sometimes get with large sums of money as well as how a family can still be a family even though it's noticeably dysfunction (if the psychological stats are correct well over half of American families are dysfunctional).<br /><br />Based on a novel of the same name by  Kaui Hart Hemmings.The budget for this film was $20M and it made a bit over $82M at the Box Office. 0439023521|4.0|There may be little point reviewing The Hunger Games. My readers usually fall into two categories - those who already love Suzanne Collins' mega-selling trilogy, and those who have consciously decided not to read it. But I would like to address a sub-section of the latter group: those who only saw the movie, but think they have experienced the story.<br /><br />They haven't.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong; it's a good movie. Convincing performances, a strong screenplay, et cetera. But the book was more than just plot and dialogue. The book was Katniss' hollow belly as the Capitol starved her and her family. The book was her mounting dread as she prepared for the Games, and her terror as she played them. The book was her grief and rage as good people were slaughtered around her for no reason at all. The book was her Mockingjay pin; not just what it looked like, but what it represented.<br /><br />Film adaptations make the sights and sounds of a story much more real, but the themes and sensations are inevitably diluted to almost nothing. I have every reason to hate The Hunger Games - it completely overshadowed the US release of my own distopian action novel, The Lab - but even so, I'm urging you to read the trilogy. The movie is a fun way to spend a couple of hours, but only the book can make you understand what the fuss was about.

0486278077|3.0|Normally, I would love a Gothic novel, even if it flaunts conventions and is highlighted by long-winded descriptions of proper gentility.  However, The Picture of Dorian Gray gets bogged down with trifles too often, which is distracting. There is an air of stuffiness and superficiality that becomes a little tiresome.<br /><br />Also, there are few redeeming characters in the novel, as the principal ones are nauseating. Take Lord Henry for instance. His long-winded philosophies and monologues dominate a good deal of the book; rather than adding much to the story, they become heavy-handed, like a point is being shoved in our face too often. And, then there is Dorian. So overdramatic and high-maintenance. Everything revolves around him and his precious little world. I get that he is supposed to be vain and materialistic, but there's little sympathy for him at all, especially when you realize he's more about forgetting his sins than actually repenting them. I realize that Wilde is philosophizing through his characters and the plot, but the means with which he goes about this is tedious.<br /><br />Still, there are redeeming aspects to the novel. Wilde does give us a moral to take away from the reading experience, as the Faustian angle of selling one's soul for beauty becomes apparent in Dorian's life. As Dorian ultimately chooses vanity over spirit and conscience, he sets the wheels of fate in motion. With devil in disguise Lord Henry egging him on, he gradually sees the portrait embody his tarnished soul: vanity, pleasures, sins. Wilde does give the book a very Gothic vibe. Dorian's portrait almost seems alive with grotesqueness, something horrible and monstrous hiding behind that sneer.<br /><br />While I did enjoy the Gothic aspects and the moral to Wilde's novel, I didn't like this novel as much as others.

ADAM's rusty nail of a rasp and gutsy riff-raff bolstered his breakthrough smash CUTS LIKE A KNIFE, the fired up TINA TURNER duet IT'S ONLY LOVE, and nostalgic singalong SUMMER OF '69, the latter two pulled from his flawless high water mark album RECKLESS; it all sounded familiar yet somehow fresh at the same time. 1434404374|5.0|She wasn't a Dame of the British Empire or the Queen of Crime when \\"The Mysterious Affair at Styles\\" was written in 1917. She was simply Agatha Miller Christie (1890-1976) whose book was not published until 1920 by the Bodley Head Press in Great Britain. The book is in the \\"cozy crime\\" genteel genre of British detective fiction which came to the fore in the between war years \\"the Golden Age of Detective Fiction.\\"<br />  The Plot: Captain Arthur Hastings (a good friend of Poirot he resembles Dr. Watson in the Sherlock Holmes works) is recuperating in Essex from injuries sustained in World War I. He visits John Cavendish an old chum of his from public school days. Soon after his arrival, Hastings learns of the murder by poison of Cavendish's stepmother. She had recently married an adventurer by the name of Alfred Inglethorpe. Among the suspects of her murder are John and and his brother Lawrence (he has practiced medicine in th past); Mary Cavendish the unhappy wife of John; Cynthia Murdoch a young relative of old Mrs. Inglethorpe and and Dr. Bauerstein a German born physician.  No one is able to solve the crime until the arrival of Monsieur Hercule Poirot a Belgian refugee from German aggresion. The novel follows a pattern Christie was often to use in turning out her novels. A closed room in which the victim is found; poison as the means of murder and a restricted group of suspects who come from upper class backgrounds.<br />  The novel is a fun perusal as the reader matches wits with Hercule Poiort and his \\"little grey cells.\\" The book is a great introduction to Agatha Christie. This is a fine novel of detection and crime. Enjoy it for a fun read!

0307719219|2.0|I agree with most of the other negative reviews I have read here.I think the thesis presented is interesting and probably has an element of truth to it.  That being said, I cannot give this book an overall good review.  Since many of the other reviews have pointed out so many of the flaws that I agree with, I won't repeat those (except for one).  As a professional historian, I will add only two comments, one a repetition of something another reviewer said (worth repeating because I find that it says so much about this book, what it lacks, and what it's purposes seem to be), and another that I haven't read here that I think is necessary.  First, I find it amazing and suspicious that the authors seem to have either no concern and/or interest in exploring \\"extractive\\" institutions in our very own current society. Let's see...as an example....um...maybe the financial services industry!!! Second, a much better and also recent book on this huge subject is, \\"Why the West Rules: For Now\\" by Ian Morris.  Unlike the \\"hedgehog\\" (God bless Isaiah Berlin! :))nature of this book, Morris, though he has a pretty clear thesis, does try to synthesize a number of possible explanations in with it (while maintaining criticisms of some of these theories).  For instance, he does not reject geographical explanations out of hand, but incorporates them in a way that makes them one part of a larger explanation of why some nations are wealthy and some are not. So Morris includes geography without strawman arguments against it, but in a nuanced and complex way that makes geography only part of the story.  This approach is much more scholarly and objective (and the book is highly readable, by the way), and by incorporating many of the other theses on this subject in order to promote his own, he shows himself much more of a \\"fox\\", in the best way possible.  Also, for what it's worth, Morris is both a historian and archaeologist from Stanford, specific credentials more conducive to this subject than the authors' in question here.  In a nutshell, read \\"Why the West Rules: For Now\\" if you want a much more plausible, fair-minded, objective, and interesting examination of this subject and skip \\"Why Nations Fail\\" (I wish I had read only the former and not both...I can't get those hours back!) -- Christian Jardine

B002MQYOFW|5.0|I'm not really giving just this first of three books 5 stars... I'm giving the trilogy a 5-star rating altogether.  The book was recommended to me by a young woman at work who mentioned that her father (my age) had \\"borrowed\\" the book from her and wouldn't give it back.  Now this intrigued me, because this is a very bright, articulate girl, and so I had to assume her father was likely no intellectual slouch either.  I also found it curious that a YA-rated book would get this level of accolade from a more mature crowd... so I decided to give it a try.  Wow.  I read copiously, and yet SELDOM do I ever make the statement that \\"I couldn't put it down\\" or that \\"I read until 4am\\".  I made both those statements while reading these 3 books.  Brilliantly-drawn characters with great depth; it was easy to become caught up in the drama in each of their lives.  Even the \\"2nd-string\\" characters -- like the community families, etc -- were developed enough that you remembered them throughout the entire ordeal.  If anything, the author drew the lead characters with almost TOO MUCH maturity for their ages (just the opposite of my remarks on the horrible trilogy of Natusch's that I just reviewed).  Intriguing plot, snappy dialogue, plenty of action... the author did seem to run out of steam a bit at the end, but it's completely forgiveable, given the whirlwind pace maintained throughout the first 2 books.  Ms. Collins is definitely an author on whom to keep your eye... which certainly shouldn't be too difficult to do with the acclaim she's garnering (and the movie recently released) with this superb offering.  Can't wait to read more!

B007I2BZIE|5.0|The above comment isn't of a derogatory nature.....no, not at all!! I'm still trying to figure out what just hit me, and see if I can put into words how great this CD is. This CD arrived in my mailbox yesterday, and I immediately opened it and passively listened it at dinner with the kids. Of course, I was 'hearing' it rather than 'listening' to it for that hour or so. In an almost reckless fashion, I had 3 stars in mind if I was going to make the mistake of reviewing it quickly. Instead, me and the kids took a road trip today, and I was able to really focus on the songs while driving, and conclude that I was listening to the best Rush album since Moving Pictures, and I'm confident with that assessment. I say this because this album shows what patience and careful craftsmanship can do; the songs are 'tight' (very little deviation in sound from one to the next, which is common for concept albums) and very robust, especially the song HEADLONG FLIGHT, which may be Neil Peart's best work since TOM SAWYER. While melodies don't initially jump out of these songs, they are nonetheless there and aren't indulgent. Basically, these songs have that 'movement' to them, and tell a great story amid the fast and sometimes furious tempo. Geddy Lee has his bass thumping more than ever, and Neil has the energy of a 20 year old, while Alex and his guitars are having the time of their lives. The standout tracks: every track. The REAL standout tracks: CARAVAN, BU2B, THE WRECKERS, HEADLONG FLIGHT, and THE GARDEN. The latter is a heartfelt slower song that has the listener rooting for these guys and admiring their talent and versatility. THE WRECKERS has an addictive melody (the only exception on this album). All of the tracks have that 'feel' to them, and have me shaking my head and concluding that these guys have reached full maturation, and not losing a thing, but rather gaining momentum. I think that this trio is just trying to have fun these days, and it's showing up in the songs; that is, the quality of them are high, and the fact that they're taking their time between albums these days is another huge reason for my predicted success of this album. I think this album will go platinum, which hasn't happened in a while. I will not attribute bigger advertising for the success, but rather word of mouth in how good this album is. And finally.......it's time to tell the harsh critics of Rush \\"enough is enough\\" and perhaps they will finally give credit where credit is due and first  acknowledge how great this album is, then realize that Rush has influenced so many bands who are already in the Hall. I'm sure Metallica (big Rush fans) have already listened to this album, and think that this album is stellar, and Rolling Stone will have to come forth and fess up that they've done a great disservice to this band for too long. B007L96VCY|5.0|'Ram' is an astonishment. Considering the brilliance of music during the early '70s by the like of Carole King & Elton John (+ Messrs. Harrison & Lennon), 'Ram' creates its own genre of magic. The tone, mood, & feel of the songs unify to present Paul building upon the 'McCartney' album to new heights. Despite the co-credit of ownership, the voice of the record is definitely Paul's although Linda's harmonies do shine in songs such as 'Dear Boy' & 'Uncle Albert/Admiral Halsey'. Shades of the past sonically appear in the horns of 'Long-Haired Lady' (reminescent of 'Mother Nature's Son') & the reprise of the title track. McCartney's sense of strident rhythm bolsters his melodies in 'Too Many People' & 'Back Seat Of My Car' with some superb singing thrown in for good measure. The unveiled treasure with this edition lies within the drumming/percussion work of Denny Seiwell. He locks with the McCartneys so well that it is little surprise that he remained with them for some time following 'Ram'. It is the sheer variety of style that gives 'Ram' its lustre which in turn makes it unique. To consider that 'Uncle Albert/Admiral Halsey' was such a huge hit mirrors musical bravery (imagine a song such as this being released now) as well as wonderful imagination that was filled with surprise and joy. Enjoy 'Ram' for everything that it is: an album that welcomes everyone with good cheer, variety, originality, and a happiness shared between the listener with Paul and Linda McCartney.
